class {\bfseries Plan\+Util}
\end{DoxyCompactItemize}


\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
Manages a flight plan or kinematic trajectory as a sequence of 4D vectors (three dimensions of space and time). Acceleration zones in a kinematic plan are defined by appending acceleration values to the beginning point of that zone. 

This class assumes that (1) the points are added in increasing time, (2) all point times are 0 or positive, (3) there are no duplicate point times. 

Points that \char`\"{}overlap\char`\"{} with existing points are deemed as redundant and will not be included in the \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan}{Plan}}. Two points overlap if they are within both a minimum distance and time of each other (as defined by min\+Dt). 

Kinematic plans can be constructed algorithmically. One way to do this is using the Util.\+Traj\+Gen.\+make\+Kinematic\+Plan() method to construct a kinematic \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan}{Plan}} core from a linear one. 

Furthermore this version of the \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan}{Plan}} assumes that any points between a beginning and paired end TCP will have constant acceleration (or turn radius). These values will be derived from the beginning and end points. It is not recommended that these Plans be directly modified. Rather the (linear) Plans they are based on should be modified and new kinematic Plans be generated from those. 

Acceleration regions are delineated by BOT, EOT, BGS, EGS, BVS, EVS trajectory change points (TCPs). In general, the end TCPS points are not considered to be part of the maneuver. All acceleration regions of the same type must be distinct and not overlap. Acceleration begin TCP points contain meta data including acceleration and initial velocity. For other points, velocities are inferred from surrounding points. 

See An Efficient Universal Trajectory Language, NASA/\+TM-\/2017-\/219669, Sept 2017.

Typical Usage\+: 
\begin{DoxyEnumerate}
\item create a \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan}{Plan}} from a linear \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan}{Plan}} using Trajectory\+Gen.\+make\+Plan( ... ) 
\item compute position as a function of time using Plan.\+position(t) 
\end{DoxyEnumerate}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily double larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::calc\+Radius (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{i }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Calculates a radius (great circle distance from center to BOT, i.\+e. surface radius). It uses center and BOT position to calculate the radius.

~\newline


Note it is usually preferable to get the radius from the \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_abe53a15bd2853bc7383a4a1c4e4cbc9e}{signed\+Radius}} method

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}} larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::closest\+Point (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_position}{Position}} \&}]{p }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Experimental This returns a \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}} on the plan that is closest to the given position. If more than one point are closest horizontally, the closer vertically is returned. If more than one have the same horizontal and vertical distances, the first is returned.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}} larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::closest\+Point (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{start,  }\item[{int}]{end,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_position}{Position}} \&}]{p,  }\item[{bool}]{horiz\+Only,  }\item[{double}]{max\+Hdist }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Experimental This returns a \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}} on the plan within the given segment range that is closest to the given position. If more than one point are closest horizontally, the closer vertically is returned. If more than one have the same horizontal and vertical distances, the first is returned. If start \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= end, this returns an INVALID point


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em start} & start point \\
\hline
{\em end} & end point \\
\hline
{\em p} & position to check against \\
\hline
{\em horiz\+Only} & if true, only consider horizontal distances, if false, also compare vertical distances if the closest points on 2 segments are within max\+Hdist of each other \\
\hline
{\em max\+Hdist} & only used if horiz\+Only is false\+: compare vertical distances if candidate points are within this range of each other \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
closest point 
\end{DoxyReturn}

Experimental Return the closest geometric point on a plan to a reference point, as measured as a Euclidean 3D norm from each linear segment. (Kinematic turns are not accounted for in this distance calculation.) This may produce unexpected results if a kinematic segment includes a turn {$\ge$} 180 degrees or a vertical segment that crosses over itself.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}} larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::closest\+Point\+Horiz (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_position}{Position}} \&}]{p }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Experimental Returns the (first) point on the plan that has the smallest horizontal distance from the reference point. If the closest point horizontally happens to occur on a 0 gs segment, it will return the point on the segment with the closest altitude. This will attempt to allow for curved turns in a kinematic plan.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}} larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::closest\+Point\+Horiz (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{seg,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_position}{Position}} \&}]{p }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Experimental Return the \char`\"{}closest\char`\"{} point on a segment to position p. This will only use horizontal (2d) distance calculations unless the segment\textquotesingle{}s ground speed is (nearly) zero, in which case it will use altitude to determine the closest point. ~\newline
 This will attempt to allow for curved turns (if kinematic). If multiple points are equally closest, it will return the first such point.

Create new plan from existing using points from index \char`\"{}first\+Ix\char`\"{} to index \char`\"{}last\+Ix\char`\"{}. This is a \char`\"{}raw\char`\"{} cut, no attention is given to TCPs.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily double larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::get\+First\+Real\+Time (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

This returns the time for the first non-\/virtual point in the plan. Usually this is the same as \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a7d52a6440c070795261b67edcde9390a}{get\+First\+Time()}}, and this should only be called if there is a known special handling of virtual points, as it is less efficient. If there are 0 non-\/virtual points in the plan, this logs an error and returns 0.\+0 \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
first time 
\end{DoxyReturn}

Return the name of this plan (probably the aircraft name). \mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a51dc9fd7effbe3d962a2555691101926}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a51dc9fd7effbe3d962a2555691101926}} 
\index{larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}!getIndex@{getIndex}}
\index{getIndex@{getIndex}!larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getIndex()}{getIndex()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily int larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::get\+Index (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{tm }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Return the index of the point that matches the provided time. If the result is negative, then the given time corresponds to no point. A negative result gives information about where the given time does enter the list. If the (negative) result is i, then the given time corresponds to a time between indexes -\/i-\/2 and -\/i-\/1. For example, if times are \{0.\+0, 1.\+0, 2.\+0, 3.\+0, 4.\+0\}\+: 
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item get\+Index(-\/3.\+0) == -\/1 -- before index 0 
\item get\+Index(1.\+0) == 1 -- at index 1 
\item get\+Index(1.\+5) == -\/3 -- between index 1 (-\/i-\/2) and 2 (-\/i-\/1) 
\item get\+Index(3.\+4) == -\/5 -- between index 3 (-\/i-\/2) and 4 (-\/i-\/1) 
\item get\+Index(16.\+0) == -\/6 -- after index 4 (-\/i-\/2) 
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em tm} & a time \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the index of the time, or negative if not found. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_aa45dbc5c1568659033c0d287a4c48432}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_aa45dbc5c1568659033c0d287a4c48432}}

If the time for point 0 is 10.\+0 and the time for point 1 is 20.\+0, then get\+Segment(10.\+0) will produce 0, get\+Segment(15.\+0) will produce 0, and get\+Segment(20.\+0) will produce 1. \mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a7b4fb4937dffc644abc6e4c1fdde2d26}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a7b4fb4937dffc644abc6e4c1fdde2d26}}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a84f9e71e7cca5107f74025903a24cadc}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a84f9e71e7cca5107f74025903a24cadc}} 
\index{larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}!mkGsConstant@{mkGsConstant}}
\index{mkGsConstant@{mkGsConstant}!larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mkGsConstant()}{mkGsConstant()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::mk\+Gs\+Constant (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{wp1,  }\item[{int}]{wp2,  }\item[{double}]{gs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Make a new plan with constant ground speed from wp1 to wp2. \begin{DoxyVerb}  200     200     200     200     200
\end{DoxyVerb}
 0 -\/-\/--- 1 -\/-\/--- 2 -\/-\/--- 3 -\/-\/--- 4 -\/-\/--- 5

mk\+Gs\+Constant(p, 1, 3, 500)

200 500 500 200 200 200 0 -\/-\/--- 1 -\/-\/--- 2 -\/-\/--- 3 -\/-\/--- 4 -\/-\/--- 5

Note that if wp1 == wp2 no change is made.

Note\+: If the initial plan has zero ground speed segments, then the final plan may have points removed.

Note. This method can handle kinematic models, but it may result in loss of velocity continuity

{\em wp1} & starting index \\

{\em wp2} & ending index \\

{\em gs} & new ground speed \\

\end{DoxyParams}

\index{larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}!position@{position}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{position()}{position()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_position}{Position}} larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::position (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{t }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Return a linear interpolation of the position at the given time. If the time is beyond the end of the plan and get\+Extend() is true, then the position is extrapolated after the end of the plan. An error is set if the time is before the beginning of the plan.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_position}{Position}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_velocity}{Velocity}} $>$ larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::position\+Velocity (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{t,  }\item[{bool}]{linear }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Compute position and velocity at time t

Note that the calculation proceeds in steps. First, the 2D path is determined. This gives a final position and final track. Then ground speed is computed. Finally vertical speed is computed.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a12f44c0aa87d033b589a9178fca14b19}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a12f44c0aa87d033b589a9178fca14b19}}

\index{removeIfRedundant@{removeIfRedundant}!larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{removeIfRedundant()}{removeIfRedundant()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [3/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily int larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::remove\+If\+Redundant (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{ix,  }\item[{bool}]{trkF,  }\item[{bool}]{gsF,  }\item[{bool}]{vsF,  }\item[{double}]{min\+Trk,  }\item[{double}]{min\+Gs,  }\item[{double}]{min\+Vs,  }\item[{bool}]{repair }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Remove point from plan if it passes all specified tests (indicated by flags)

Note\+: This method can remove a \char`\"{}named\char`\"{} point, but will not remove a TCP or Alt\+Preserve Note\+: A point is not redundant if it is a TCP, is Alt\+Preserve, has information or a name or if there is a significant change in velocity as determined by parameters min\+Trk, min\+Gs, and min\+Vs,


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ix} & index of interest \\
\hline
{\em trkF} & track flag\+: perform track continuity test \\
\hline
{\em gsF} & ground speed flag\+: perform ground speed continuity test \\
\hline
{\em vsF} & vertical speed flag\+: perform vertical speed continuity test \\
\hline
{\em min\+Trk} & minimum track \\
\hline
{\em min\+Gs} & minimum ground speed \\
\hline
{\em min\+Vs} & minimum vertical speed \\
\hline

{\footnotesize\ttfamily void larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::repair\+Gs\+Consistency (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Attempt to fix (gs) acceleration inconsistencies in this plan by adjusting accel values and/or point times. \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
new plan with fixed inconsistencies, or null if unfixable. This new plan may have warnings (informational, possibly not concerning) or errors (possibly concerning). 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a868efd2d14145705ba10364e7f79df96}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a868efd2d14145705ba10364e7f79df96}} 
\index{larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}!repairGsContinuity@{repairGsContinuity}}
\index{repairGsContinuity@{repairGsContinuity}!larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{repairGsContinuity()}{repairGsContinuity()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::repair\+Gs\+Continuity (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{ix\+BGS,  }\item[{int}]{ix\+EGS,  }\item[{double}]{vo,  }\item[{double}]{vf,  }\item[{double}]{max\+Gs\+Accel }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Given a gs accel zone and modified starting and ending velocities, change the acceleration and internal points\textquotesingle{} times so that it is continuous with the velocities into and out of the BGS-\/\+EGS zone


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em p} & \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_plan}{Plan}} to be fixed \\
\hline
{\em ix\+BGS} & index of BGS \\
\hline
{\em ix\+EGS} & index of EGS \\
\hline
{\em vo} & target gs\+Out at ix\+BGS \\
\hline
{\em vf} & target gs\+In at ix\+EGS \\
\hline
{\em max\+Gs\+Accel} & maximum gs acceleration allowed\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
NOTE\+: given d, vo, vf calculate a and dt using two equations\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}   d = vo*t + 0.5*a*t*t
   vf = vo + a*t
\end{DoxyVerb}
 NOTE\+: if the calculated acceleration exceeds max\+Gs\+Accel, then add error to plan \mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a34545f13f0a8a1fbb03bb7fad427d789}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_a34545f13f0a8a1fbb03bb7fad427d789}}

Attempt to replace the i-\/th point with the given \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}}. If successful, this returns the index of the new point (which may change because of a new time relative to the old point). This method returns an error if the given index is out of bounds or a warning if the new point overlaps with (and replaces) a different existing point.

Restores \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_traj_gen}{Traj\+Gen}} generation parameters back to default values \mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_af15ab219b6e266ecbc5caf6276cbe385}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_af15ab219b6e266ecbc5caf6276cbe385}} 
\index{larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}!setNavPoint@{setNavPoint}}
\index{setNavPoint@{setNavPoint}!larcfm::Plan@{larcfm::Plan}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setNavPoint()}{setNavPoint()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily int larcfm\+::\+Plan\+::set\+Nav\+Point (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{i,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}} \&}]{v }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Attempt to replace the i-\/th point with the given \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_nav_point}{Nav\+Point}}. The \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_tcp_data}{Tcp\+Data}} from the old point is retained. If successful, this returns the index of the new point (which may change because of a new time relative to the old point). This method returns -\/1 and sets an error if the given index is out of bounds or a warning if the new point overlaps with (and replaces) a different existing point.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em i} & the index of the point to be replaced \\
\hline

Attempt to replace the i-\/th point\textquotesingle{}s tcp data with the given data. The navpoint from the old point is retained. If successful, this returns the index of the new point. This method returns -\/1 and sets an error if the given index is out of bounds.

Sets the radius of point i (in a linear plan)

Note\+: This is used by \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_traj_gen_a76ac1994430b61a4c4ff0203e81048e6}{Traj\+Gen.\+make\+Kinematic\+Plan}} to create a turn with a user-\/specified radius rather than one generated from a bank angle and ground speed.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em i} & index of point \\
\hline
{\em radius} & value to be set\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Note\+: the radius may be either signed or unsigned. The \mbox{\hyperlink{classlarcfm_1_1_traj_gen}{Traj\+Gen}} generators use the absolute value of this parameter. Note that the radius stored in a BOT must be signed. This is done in the turn generators. \mbox{\Hypertarget{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_ad44d529e2022eb0a249ebbeecaf66652}\label{classlarcfm_1_1_plan_ad44d529e2022eb0a249ebbeecaf66652}}
